@ Chief of Campus Police James
LaPaglia reviews all reports prior 
to release.
@ Only three people on The Tar­
tan staff see the reports: the Edi­
tor in Chief, the News Editor, and 
the staffwriter typing the report.
@ All personal names of com­
plainants, victims, suspects, and 
fraternity names are omitted from 
the printed report. Ethnic descrip­
tions and other personal details 
are given only in the context of 
complete descriptions.
• Not every incident that occurs 
on campus appears in the report.
Compiled by 
RYAN SCHILLING

BOOKS ARE MONEY 
GUARD AGAINST THEFT
We will pay up to 50% of the book price 
providing the textbook:
• Is being used on this campus.
• Is needed to fill the bookstore's quota.
• Is in reusable condition.
Example: You paid $46.00 for a textbook; 
we will pay $23.00 or 50%.
U.Sgovego
• For books not needed on this campus but 
having national demand, up to 35% of the 
new price may be paid.
• Discontinued books are shipped to a 
wholesaler who recycles them to other 
colleges and universities where they are 
needed.
• Old editions have no national value.
LE
?1&1&21a
• Recycling your books is good for the 
environment and lowers the price of textbooks.
• Books with writing or highlighting may have 
value.
• The book prices are determined by the 
publishers.
• Wholesale prices are based on national supply 
and demand.
• Copies in poor condition will be deducted 
appropriately.
• Old editions have no value and cannot be 
purchased.

---------------------------------------------------

As we end another school year, 
The Tartan board once again 
awards CMU’s best and worst of 
the past year with Thistles and 
Thoms.
The first Thistle goes to the two 
new buildings of campus — the 
University Center and Roberts 
Engineering Hall — and to those 
responsible for such timely and 
on-budget completions. The UC, 
which opened in August has added 
a number of valuable facilities 
and increased interaction be­
tween students.
A Thistle goes to CMU’s new 
president, Dr. Jared Cohon, and 
to the Presidential Search Com­
mittee for their efforts in finding 
a president-elect before gradua­
tion. The committee receives an­
other Thistle for attempts to so­
licit student input during the 
search.
A Thom goes to students for 
living up to their apathetic repu­
tations and their lack of interest 
in forums set up to gain student 
opinion, such as the Student 
Liason Committee for the Presi­
dential search.
A Thom also goes to the closing 
of the Co-op, with no current plans 
to make use of empty space or the 
space left when WRCT moved in 
to the UC. Another Thorn goes to 
the new child care center on the 
first floor of Morewood Gardens
— that space should have been 
used for student facilities.
Thorns go to the lack of flexibil­
ity in first-year meal plans, which 
force students to eat at Highlander 
regardless of their preference.
A Thorn goes to a shortage of on- 
campus housing facilities, and the 
University Housing Office’s tem­
porary solutions such as placing 
freshmen in rooms at the Hamp­
ton Inn and paying upperclass­
men to house freshmen on their 
floors for the first few weeks of 
school. The UHO also gets a 
Thistle for the improvements in 
their web-based interface, keep­
ing students up-to-date on room 
availability during Room Draw.
A Thistle goes to the implemen­
tation of on-line registration in 
CIT and CS with hopes of expand­
ing the service to other depart­
ments in the near future.
A Thistle to goes to the HUB’s 
Web site, which allows students 
to view their grades, enrollment 
status, student account and to 
make changes to address infor­
mation. A huge Thorn to the con­
tinued inefficiency of the HUB 
office.
Once again Parking receives a 
Thorn. Parking is still unavail­
able to most of the campus com­
munity at any given time of the 
day. With plans for another new 
building on campus, the Univer­
sity needs to rethink its current 
parking facilities.
A Thistle goes to the first an­
nual Mosaic Women’s Conference 
and the Women’s Festival for pro­
viding outlets to discuss women’s 
issues on campus. Hopefully, 
CMU will continue its efforts to 
address the academic and social 
concerns of CMU women.
A Thorn goes to CPA’s Wats:on? 
Festival of the Arts for excluding 
other colleges from the 
celebration’s events and for fos­
tering isolation among colleges.
A Thom goes to the weather 
during this year’s Carnival. Or­
ganizations were forced to build 
booths in near freezing weather;
the final day of Buggy was can­
celled dues to rain. Thistles goes 
to all those who maintained their 
enthusiasm and made Carnival 
one of the most memorable three- 
day period for the campus com­
munity.
A Thistle to AB for bringing 
great bands to CMU this year and 
Thistles all around for the Spring 
Carnival Committee for organiz­
ing yet another great Carnival.
Thistles to Spirit of Skibo, for 
promoting school spirit at foot­
ball games. Thanks for attack­
ing the age-old problem of stu­
dent apathy and for actually 
making a difference.
Thorns go The Student Union 
for not publishing consistently 
and for failing to request Senate 
funding for next year. As it 
stands The Student Union, 
which has always acted as an­
other voice for students on cam­
pus is no longer in publication.
A Thistle to Student Senate 
becoming a more active organi­
zation through the efforts of Stu­
dent Body President Bryon 
Krug. Krug receives a Thistle 
for creating the Student Gov­
ernment newsletter and venues 
for more student involvement in 
Student Senate. Senate and A 
Phi O get multiple Thorns for 
poorly planning and executing 
Student Government elections 
this year.
A Thorn goes to the new double 
major registration policy which 
limits prioritization to majors 
only. A Thorn to the administra­
tion for ignoring not only stu­
dent responses to the new policy, 
but to complaints from faculty 
and administration from indi­
vidual colleges.
A Thistle goes the Undergradu­
ate Research Initiative for the 
expansion of SURG programs 
offered to students, especially 
by increasing the number of 
grants given to arts and humani­
ties projects. CMU is know as a 
prestigious research institution
— it’s important that under­
graduates be able to take part in 
that experience.
Thistles go to the Hunt Library 
renovations and the installation 
of the Baker Hall elevator. 
Thorns go to the fences around 
the Cut.
A Thistle goes to the 
President’s office for continuing 
to sponsor “Take Our Daughter’s 
to Work Day.”
Thorns go to Skibo Coffeehouse 
for poor service and a lack of 
atmosphere. Students still have 
no real “hangout” similar to 
Skibo’s Scotland Yard.
Thistles go to recent cluster 
and server upgrades and Data 
Communications Network 2000.
A Thistle to the removal of the 
ugly office space trailers outside 
Baker and Porter Hall.
Thistles also go out to the foot­
ball team for winning their last 
seven games in a row, ending 
the year with a 7-2 record. Se­
nior Rich Bodnar also gets a 
Thistle for scoring his 1000 ca­
reer point this semester.
Finally, many Thistles to se­
niors graduating this year. We 
hope to learn from your experi­
ences and hear of your successes 
in the near future.
Good luck to returning stu­
dents, faculty, staff and admin­
istration as we make our way 
through another year.

The Tartan is the student newspaper of Carnegie Mellon University. It is a weekly 
newspaper published by students during the fall and spring semesters, at no cost to 
members of the University community. It is 
printed by Western Pennsylvania Printing, Inq. 
Subscriptions are available for the semester 
or academic year. The editorials appearing 
at the beginning of the opinion section are 
the official opinion of The Tartan editorial 
board. Columns and political cartoons are 
the opinions of individual creators. The Tartan reserves the right to reject or 
condense any column or political cartoon. 
Letters to the Editor are opinions of authors 
who are usually, but not necessarily, 
members of the University community. A 
letter intended for publication must be signed and include the writer's address and pnone 
number for verification. Names may be withheld upon request. The Tartan requests 
that letters be no longer than 500 words. The Tartan reserves the right to condense
it deems unfit for publication. -----------

E Don’t Cheat Yourself Out of an Education
“Under stress or time pressure people may rationalize 
that no one is hurt if a student “takes a shortcut.” But 
each person’s attitudes and actions contribute to our 
individual and community standards. Giving in to 
these urges also means giving up a measure of per­
sonal integrity. Bit by bit, what may seem like small Ul ethical compromises sacrifice the integrity of our aca­
demic community. Promoting academic integrity is 
the responsibility of the entire Carnegie Mellon com­
munity.”
Promoting Academic Integrity: 
A Discussion Guide for the CMU Community*
Carnegie Mellon Academic Integrity CasesFall 1995-Fall 1996

The devil visited a young lawyer's office and made him an offer.
“I can arrange some things for you,” the devil said. “I’ll increase your income five-fold. 
Your partners will love you; your clients will respect you; you'll have four months of vaca­
tion each year and live to be a hundred. All I require in return is that your wife’s soul, your 
children’s souls and their children’s souls must rot in hell for eternity.”
The lawyer thought for a moment and said, “What's the catch?”

the heart of it.

on the map!

by Roger and Salem Salloom ©1996
I have a very big 65 gallon 
fish tank.
I only have one chubby little 
goldfish who slowly waddles 
around alone.
Because of the glass angles, 
sometimes, I can't even see 
Beebles.
Beebles rubs his side 
against the stone a lot.
I asked the clerk at the pet
store:
Why does my fish keep 
rubbing against the stone?
If I buy another fish and my 
fish falls in love, v/ill Beebles be 
happier than when Beebles was 
alone?
The clerk thre w me out of the
store.
Hail to all who waddle alone!

DH FFEWr 11,1.11 I ramane
movies you may have seen before....
By GREG MARCKS
Thursday, May 1
The Last Picture Show
This 1971 B&W Peter Bogdanovich film is about a 
small Texas town in the late ’40s. Two high school 
chums, Sonny and Duane, worry about their fu­
tures. Well, Duane doesn’t worry so much, because 
his girlfriend is hot and her dad is rich. If he marries 
her, he can move to Easy Street.
Then Sam the Lion enters the picture, tearing 
people limb from limb and causing mass hysteria. 
The local economy collapses, and the second-run 
movie theather shows its last show. This infuriates 
Sonny, who decides to take matters into his own 
hands. He assembles a vigilante group who slay the 
snarling beast, and then they dance around the 
burning corpse.
At 7:30, 10 pm, and 12:30 am 
In DH 2210
Friday, May 2
Beavis & Butt-head Do 
America
Not since the Griswolds packed up the family truckster 
has there been such a successful lampoon of America. 
“Huh, huh. Huh, huh, huh. He said lamb poon.” 
“Shut up, ass goblin! I’m trying to itch my bunghole. 
I am Cornholio! Are you threatening me? You want 
to take away my bunghole!”
This movie has it all: jokes and a plot! In search of 
their missing TV, the B-boys are mistaken for hitmen 
(yeah right) and are sent to Las Vegas to do some 
chick who puts a secret weapon in Beavis’s pants 
(make that two). This, of course, leads to full cavity 
searches for all — deep and hard!
At dusk (Around 9:30 pm)
On the Grassy Knoll
Scream, a.k.a. Scary Movie
Wes Craven parodies himself in this terrificomic 
exposé of the horror genre. Courtney Cox is a tabloid 
reporter bent on stopping a psychotic killer from 
stalking Drew Barrymore, who is still freaked out 
from being in E.T.
At 11:30 pm 
On the Grassy Knoll
Saturday, May 3
The Chamber
Bo knows murder. That’s right, folks, everyone’s 
favorite all-around athlete is back and more knowl­
edgeable than ever in this John Grisham-based 
flick. Originally titled More Lawyer Crap, the name 
was changed as a clever way of refèrring to a court 
anteroom and a place to insert a bullet.
James Foley, the man who successfully kept Al 
Pacino from the center of every frame in Glengarry 
Glen Ross, returns to do battle with Gene “Lex 
Luthor” Hackman, Faye “Evelyn Mulwray” Dunaway, 
and Chris “SnivelingTwit” O’Donnell in atrial where 
a lawyer represents his own grandfather, a Klansman 
accused of the murder of two Jewish boys.
At 7:30, 10 pm, and 12:30 am 
In McConomy
Sunday, May 4
The Return of the Living Dead
Yes, those ambulatory oxymorons are back! Two 
crazy kids accidentally spread deadly gas into a 
medical supply warehouse, which any good Betty 
Crocker will tell you is a sure-fire way to raise the 
dead. Voted the most stereotypical film of 1985.
At 8, 10 pm, and midnight 
In DH 2210
Last Week’s Quote:
“Did you try staples?” — Bill Murray in Scrooged
